3.10 Bioinformatics 
 
The MGmapper (DTU) (MetaGenomics mapper) pipeline can process either single-end or paired-
end fastq files. The input fastq files can come from any data source i.e. single genome data or Meta 
genomics data from many genomes. The tool can be found here [78]   
Mapping options were such: mapping mode is paired-end; trimming of reads via cut adapt. 
Trimming parameters: minimal read length after trimming is 30 , minimum Phred quality is 30, cut 
adapt Quality base 33. Potential Phix control reads from Illumna sequencing are removed.Adapter 
sequences to be removed:  
AGATCGGAAGAGCACACGTCTGAACTCCAGTCACNNNNNNATCTCGTATGCCGTCTTC
TGCTTG 
AATGATACGGCGACCACCGAGATCACACTCTTTCCCTACACGACGCTCTTCCGATCT 
AGATCGGAAGAGCACACGTCTGAACTCCAGTCAC 
AGATCGGAAGAGCGTCGTGTAGGGAAAGAGTGTA  [78]. 
Database selection: database id”s for Beds-mode mapping 1,2. In bastmode a pair of reads can only 
map to 1 database. If pair of reads has been mapped to two or more databases then the alignment-
score sum is calculated for all databases were the paired reads have been mapped. Aligment-score 
sum= aligment-score forward read+aligment-score reverse read. The reads are assigned to a 
database, were the highest aligment-score sum is obtained. If that score is identical for two or more 
databases, then the database assignment is chosen according to witch database was specified first 
during the database selection.  
Map reads against all selected databases via “bva mem”. 
Fastq read alignment criteria: FMM value 0,8. (Fraction of Mathes plus Mismatches). MAS 
(Minimum Aligment Score for a read) 30. 
Paired-end reads are properly paired and both are present after the post-processing step.  
Clade level post-processing: Abundance cutoff (%) 0.01. Unique reads ratio 0.005) minimum ratio: 
Reads/Reads_uniq. 
Max mismatch ratio 0.01 (Maximum ratio: Edit_distance/Nucleotides) 
Fastq files were oploaded as Paired-end reads. Jobs are run in parallel using 4 cores. Max runtime in 
MGmapper 72 hours [78]. 
Assembled contig files: 
Assembled contig fasta files are made for each database selected for contig sequence assembly, via 
samtools mpileup.SNPs and INDELs are included in the contig fasta files if a variant is present at 
least 4 times and account for at least 50% of variations.Otherwise the reference sequence nucleotide 
is inserted in fasta sequence. SNP and INDEL vairants are shown as lowercase letters in contig files 
[78]. 
Output format description: 
 
39 
==PAGE:40==
Once the MGmapper server has finished running the submitted job, it will show the following 
information: 
Tables showing overall statistics with number of reads that have been read and how many remain 
after trimming 
Two tables showing number of reads that mapped to each of the databases that were selected 
Tables in blue colour with 5 lines of results for each database. Press view all to see all hits 
Tables in green colour with 5 lines of results for each database but only the most confident hits 
where flags AS and XS differ, meaning only uniquely mapped reads are shown. Press view all to 
see all hits [78]. 
All results including graphics can be viewed by downloading excel workbook result files. 
Description of the Graphical output  'Statistics' tables - one for each selected target database in 
'Bestmode' 'Database' is the collection of reference sequences like Bacteria, Human, Virus ..., that 
were used as target database for the query fastq reads. 'Ref Seq' is the specific target sequence name 
in a reference sequence Database.'Abundance (%)' is the [ read Count*100]/[(Size of reference 
sequence)*2] for paired-end reads. The factor '2' is omitted in reads are single-end reads 
'Size (bp)' is the basepair length in of the reference sequence. 'Nucleotides' is the number of bases in 
the query reads that was mapped to a specific reference sequence. 'Covered positions' are the 
number of positions in the reference sequence that was covered by at least 1 read. 'Coverage' is 
Covered positions/Size. 'Depth' is Nucleotides/Size. 'Read Count' is the number of reads mapped to 
a reference sequence. 'Read Count unique' is the number of reads, were uniquely mapped to a 
reference sequence. I.e. alignment score sum (for paired reads) is higher than any secondary 
alignments. 
'Mismatches' is the total number of edits (or mismatches) to make the reads match perfectly to the 
reference sequence. 'Description' is the header of the reference sequence.  
The last 16 columns is the taxonomy annotation and taxied for superfamily, phylum, class, order, 
family, genus, species and strain [78]. 
 
Bioinformatics on the Genomic Workbench CLC Bio( Qiagen) 
CLC Genomics Workbench – a cross-platform desktop application with a graphical user-interface 
for analyzing and visualizing next generation sequencing data incorporates cutting-edge technology 
and algorithms, while also supporting and integrating with the rest of your typical NGS workflow. 
CLC Genomics Workbench is available for Windows, Mac OS X, and Linux platforms. It includes 
a number of features within the fields of genomics, transcriptomics and epigenomics, and 
additionally it includes all the tools of CLC Main Workbench. 
License Order ID: CLC-LICENSE-9848Y-JGG69-Y004V-W4ZC5-NDR5Y valid for both the CLC 
Genomics Workbenchand the CLC Microbial Genomics Module. 
Genomics Workbench 8.5.1 her (under "get a free trial"): [79]. Microbial genomics module 
 
40 
==PAGE:41==
(Download a trial): [80]. Tutorial includ 141 pages and can be viewed on CLS BIO webpage: [80].  
Microbial genomics module-latest improvements: se Apppendix 2. 
System requirements:Windows Vista, Windows 7, Windows 8, Windows 10, Windows Server 
2008, or Windows Server 2012.Mac OS X 10.7 or later.Linux: RHEL 5.0 or later. SUSE 10.2 or 
later. Fedora 6 or later.2 GB RAM required8 GB RAM recommended.1024 x 768 display required, 
1600 x 1200 display recommended.Intel or AMD CPU required. 
 
 Raw Illumina paired end sequence data were cleaned, trimmed and mapped against reference 
sequence databases . 
General remarks: Workflows are built in Workbench and combine various tools from the toolbox 
into one analysis. Workflows can also be run in batch,  and can be distributed and installed in [81], 
[82] or [83].A workflow consists of a series of tools where the output of one tool is connected as the 
input to another tool. This way you can set up a workflow to go through (for example) read 
mapping, using the mapped reads as input for variant detection, and perform filtering of the variant 
track. Once the workflow is set up, it can be installed (either in your own Workbench, on a Server, 
or sent to a colleague) and you can then analyze a lot of samples using the same standard pipeline 
with the same reference data and parameters.  
There are a number of ways to trim sequence reads prior to assembly and mapping, including 
adapter trimming, quality trimming and length trimming. For each original read, the regions of the 
sequence to be removed for each type of trimming operation are determined independently 
according to choices made in the trim dialogs. The types of trim operations that can be performed 
are: quality trimming based on quality scores; ambiguity trimming to trim off e.g. stretches of Ns ; 
adapter trimming; base trim to remove a specified number of bases at either 3' or 5' end of the reads 
;length trimming to remove reads shorter or longer than a specified threshold. The trim operation 
that removes the largest region of the original read from either end is performed while other trim 
operations are ignored as they would just remove part of the same region.  This may occasionally 
expose an internal region in a read that has now become subject to trimming. In such cases, 
trimming may have to be done more than once.  
 
The result of the trim is a list of sequences that have passed the trim (referred to as the trimmed list 
below) and optionally a list of the sequences that have been discarded and a summary report (list of 
discarded sequences). The original data will not be changed. Map Reads to Reference: there are two 
different versions of the core mapper: one for color space data, and one for base space data. At [84] 
it is possible to find white papers with detailed benchmarks and descriptions of both algorithms. 
There are also different parameters in subsections: Selecting reads and reference; Including or 
excluding regions (masking);Mapping parameters ;Mapping paired reads; Non-specific matches; 
 
41 
==PAGE:42==
Gap placement ;Computational requirements; Reference Caching. By using CKC Genomics 
Workbench for NGS data it is possible to create   metadata and analysis results tables, identify the 
best matching reference and its taxonomy, visualizing associated metadata in the context of the 
phylogenetic tree.

==PAGE:57==
5 Discussion 
 
Results from DNA purification shows great difference in the final concentration of the total DNA, 
depending on the samples storage duration at -20°C. The fresh inoculated chicken faeces samples 
purified with Qiagen purification kit allows higher concentrations of total DNA measured by 
QIAamp DNA Stool Mini Kit compared to measurements of total DNA after purification of 
samples that have been on -20°C in one year without special freeze media. 
Results from PCR show that the fresh samples, purified by the QIAamp DNA Stool Mini Kit 
protocol provides 32,34 in average CT values from the samples inoculated with 10³ CFU and 24,88 
average CT from the samples inoculated with 10³ CFU. One-year-old samples, that have been 
stored ongoing at -20°C and purified with QIAamp DNA Stool Mini Kit DNA and Easy-DNA™ 
Kit, do not give any results from the concentration of 10³ CFU / ml.  Ct values from samples 
inoculated with 10
6
 CFU are generally higher than 30 CT from both purification methods, and are 
too high for sequencing by 8 per flow cell. There are also big differences between RCR results from 
fresh and one-year-old ongoing stored at -20°C samples, purified by using the same QIAamp DNA 
Stool Mini Kit method. Samples purified by Easy-DNA™ Kit does not give very promising CT 
values, but are however a bit higher than the samples purified by QIAamp DNA Stool Mini Kit. 
There is no obvious correlation between the amount of total DNA and Campylobacter DNA as 
determined by real-time PCR was found.  Whether a direct correlation between the amount of 
amplifiable Campylobacter DNA and the outcome of a diagnostic metagenomics analysis exists 
will be investigated further. 
It was not possible to grow Campylobacter jejuni from the frozen samples spiked with 10³ CFU 
and10
6
 CFU, so there is high probability that the Campylobacter cells collapsed and Campylobacter 
DNA degraded in the course of prolonged storage at -20°C So the large difference in CT values 
from QIAamp DNA Stool Mini Kit method can be explained by the long storage of the 
Campylobacter cells. It raises questions about how long we can keep the stool samples at -20°C) 
without special freezing media, and what kind of freeze media should be used for samples with low 
CFU / g targets. 
The choice of DNA purifications kits can also be discussed. QIAamp DNA Stool Mini Kit and 
Easy-DNA™ Kit are designed to act on the intact cells, where the first step of the two kits are 
”inhibitor removal”, therefore, our designated cells may disappear. If the first step of the 
purification is a cell lyses, we could possible store DNA in the tube, but then the level of inhibitors 
would be loud - hvis det her er hypotetisk/eventuel handling i fremtiden. Question is what kind of 
kit can be used to purify designated cells from the stool samples and especially from such a difficult 
matrix as chicken faeces? Maybe a Meta-G-Nome™ DNA Isolation Kit (Illumina) could be a 
suggestion. 
 
57 
==PAGE:58==
 
Target enrichment strategies for next-generation sequencing are dealing with compromise between 
sensitivity, specifically and uniformity for particular projects. The padlock protocol findings show 
that the production of cLPPs (complementary long padlock probes) have provided some results. 
There are bands on the gel with the right size, so we can conclude that probes design for 
Campylobacter jejuni, based on seven MLST gens for Campylobacter jejuni, is the right choice. 
Capture has worked at least to some extent. Correct band for glnA PCR1 is only in the capture on 
pure Campy DNA (10 ng/µl), but is not in the DNA isolated from faeces inoculated with 
Campylobacter jejuni.  Four from the twelve MLST captures could be confirmed (pure 
Campylobacter jejuni DNA). GlnA PCR1 band is clear on Gel1, but absent on Gel2, which points 
in the direction that the PCRs 11-22 might not have been the best. Our assay uses an excess of 
probes over the amount of target (LPP/target ratio of approximately 40:1) and following 
denaturation at higher temperature (98°C, 3 minutes) and strand separation, so probe-target 
formation may be triggered by chance over the time . An alternative but less likely hypothesis is a 
strand displacement mechanism, where two strands with partial or full complimentarily can 
hybridize to each other, displacing in the process one or more pre-hybridized strands [59].  
However, existing padlock probes construct which did not give any results on MiSeq'en, may be 
missing the insert, a set of Illumina ( MiSeq ) sequencing primer sites to machine sequencing.  
This part of the padlock method, where capture libraries are multiplex-amplified using hybrid 
primers than anneal to the probes amplification sites and Illumina sequencing adaptors and sample-
specific barcodes shall be redesigned. The new probes shall contain the Illumina specific adapters.  
There is a very few technologies on the market witch can boost target concentration of target-DNA 
for  matagenomic sequencing , so it is difficult to compare our developments to other technologies. One 
of them is Nextera Rapid Capture Custom Enrichment’s specificity based on post library preparation 
twice biotin labelling followed steptavidin beads magnetically enrichment the targeted region, that are 
hybridized to biotinylated probs. After eluation from the beads, the process is completed [85]. 
Comparing to the Nextera Rapid Capture Custom Enrichment, the process of constructing cLPPs 
directly from a PCR product allows for better quality control and is more time and cost-effective. 
Input of total DNA in Nextera Rapid Capture Custom Enrichment should be 50 ng, but padlock 
technology needs only 10 ng. Padlock technology can give cheaper and faster solution and 
maximizes coverage across increasingly larger capture products and is fully compatible with 
existing library preparation protocols used by a variety of multiplex targeted sequencing methods 
[54]. 
Bioinformatics analyses results from the MGmapper (Center for Genomic epidemiology, DTU) and 
CLC Microbial Genomics are equal and did not give any Campylobacter jejuni results on MiSeq'en.  
Concentration of our target DNA in metagenomic samples cannot be measured, therefore we cannot 
be certain at what low levels of concentration of target DNA would be sufficient for bioinformatics 
identification of strain. However, many reads from metagenomic samples come from genomes that 
 
58 
==PAGE:59==
are not in any reference database [60]. In our project we used only one method for taxonomical 
classification: sequence similarity based methods, which use the results of a sequence similarity 
search against a database of a reference set of sequences[61]. We did not use other methods such as 
sequence composition based methods, which are based on characteristics of their nucleotide 
composition (e.g. tetranucleotide usage or codon usage) [62], or hybrid methods which incorporate 
components of the first two.  Other possibilities in the further could also be marker-based methods, 
which identify species based on the occurrence of certain specific marker sequences. Composition 
methods could generate models from the reference organisms’ genomes, and would classify the 
input sequence reads based on which model(s) fit the read best. For improving classification, scores 
may be combined from both the similarity portion and the composition portion of the method for 
each prediction [63]. Another hybrid strategy, aimed at increasing speed, is to use the composition 
approach to narrow down the set of candidate organisms, and thus have the similarity search occur 
against a fraction of the original database [64]. 
Analysis of metagenomic sequences is complicated due to the complex structure of the data. 
Metagenomic analysis tends to require a large volume of data to identify meaningful results because 
of the vast amount of genomic information being sampled. Bioinformatic software development is 
one of solution for this problem. There are many web-based tools that centralize metagenome data 
management and analysis. Some of them can be investigated in further studies, in terms of 
analysing metagenom data from samples with low-number bacterial of interest (Tabel1)[65]. 
 
Table 17. Web-based metagenomic analysis resources. Adapted from [65]. 
 
 
 
 
 
59 
==PAGE:60==
6 Conclusions 
The results of this study are showing significant, almost total degradation of Campylobacter jejuni 
from long period storage at -20°C (up to one year) samples. Degradation was confirmed by Real-
time PCR and conventional cultivation on agar plates. QIAamp DNA Stool Mini Kit (Qiagen) is 
very good performing protocol regarding total DNA yield from the inoculated chicken fecal 
samples. The Padlock concept generally has problems with the existing padlock probe construct 
which gave negative results from the sample with highest inoculation level and control. False 
negative results at MiSeq'en could be explained by the fact that there were no Illumina (MiSeq) 
insert for the machine to detect the padlock probe. The bioinformatics part of study confirms that 
both platforms, MGmapper (Center for Genomic epidemiology, DTU) and CLC Microbial 
Genomics could be used for future studies for  microbial community analysis as well as tools for 
epidemiological typing of microbial isolates, but bioinformatics analysis methods are not optimized 
for samples with very low concentrations of bacteria (false negative results).  
In order to continue research it would be necessary to find new, or optimized existing DNA 
extraction procedures DNA extraction procedures and construct some new Pad Lock with the 
specific Illumina adapters. MGmapper (Center for Genomic epidemiology, DTU) and CLC 
Microbial Genomics could be used for future studies, but need to include the tools for low-
abundance bacterial strains to avoid false negative results. It would also be interesting to investigate 
correlation between the amount of amplifiable DNA, exemplified by Campylobacter, in the 
metagenomic samples, and the outcome of a diagnostic metagenomics analysis for determining the 
lowest concentration of bacteria in faecal samples, that do not give false negative results with the 
current condition of the bioinformatics tools.

9. Appendices. 
9.1. Appendix-1. Laboratory standard operating procedure for Nextera library 
prep and run setop for the Illumina MiseQ.  
 
PURPOSE: To describe the standardized laboratory protocol for whole genome sequencing of 
bacterial organisms on the MiSeq benchtop sequencer. 
 
1. 
SCOPE: To provide the PulseNet participants with a single protocol for performing Nextera 
XT library prep and MiSeq run setup, thus ensuring inter-laboratory comparability of the 
generated results. 
 
2. 
DEFINITIONS: 
2.1. WGS: Whole Genome Sequencing 
2.2. DNA: Deoxyribonucleic acid 
2.3. DNase: Deoxyribonuclenase 
2.4. PCR: Polymerase chain reaction 
2.5. CDC: Centers for Disease Control and Prevention 
2.6. SOP: Standard Operating Procedure 
2.7. ATM: Amplicon Tagment Mix 
2.8. TD: Tagment DNA Buffer 
2.9. NPM: Nextera PCR Master Mix 
2.10. RSB: Resuspension Buffer 
2.11. NT: Neutralize Tagment Buffer 
2.12. TCY: Skirted Thermocycler Plate 
2.13. NTA: Nextera XT Tagment Amplicon 
2.14. CAA: Clean Amplified Plate 
2.15. EDTA: Ethylenediaminetetraacetic acid 
2.16. NaOH: Sodium Hydroxide 
2.17. EBT: Elution Buffer with Tween 
2.18. HT1: Hybridization buffer 
2.19. PR2: Incorporation buffer 
2.20. QC: Quality Control 
 
3. RESPONSIBILITIES/PROCEDURE 
3.1. Biosafety warning: Foodborne pathogens are capable of causing serious disease. Always 
use a minimum of Biosafety level 2 practices and extreme caution when transferring and 
handling strains of this type. Work in a biological safety cabinet when handling organisms 
with a low infectious dose. Disinfect or dispose of all plastic ware and glassware that come 
in contact with the cultures in a safe manner.  
NOTE: The MiSeq Reagent Cartridges contain formamide, an aliphatic amide that is 
a potential reproductive toxin.  Ensure spent containers and unused contents are 
disposed of in accordance with governmental safety standards. 
 
3.2. Reagents, supplies and equipment needed for DNA extraction and quality control

3.4. Day 0: 
 
3.4.1. Isolate preparation 
3.4.1.1. 
Streak an isolated colony from test cultures to TSA-SB plate (or comparable 
media). Incubate cultures at 37ºC for 14-18 hrs. 
NOTE: If using the ArchivePure DNA Extraction kit, it is suggested to inoculate 
Trypticase Soy Broth.  
3.5. Day 1: 
3.5.1. DNA extraction / template preparation using the Qiagen DNeasy Blood & Tissue 
Kit 
NOTE: If using the Archive Pure DNA extraction procedure, see Appendix PNL-1. 
A minimum of 4 - 6 hours must be allocated to complete the process. 
 
3.5.1.1. 
Before beginning this procedure, first: 
3.5.1.1.1. 
Pre-heat waterbath or heat block to 56°C ± 1. 
3.5.1.1.2. 
Check DNeasy kit reagents and dilute where necessary (i.e. ethanol 
needs to be added to both wash buffers prior to the very first use). 
3.5.1.1.3. 
Prepare the elution buffer, 10 mM Tris HCl pH 8.0, as follows: 
3.5.1.1.3.1. 
Add 10 ml of 1 M Tris-HCl pH 8.0 to 990 ml molecular grade 
water. Invert several times to mix (store at 4°C). 
 
3.5.1.1.4. 
For Gram positive DNA extractions: Prepare the enzymatic lysis buffer 
(ELB):20 mM Tris, 2 mM EDTA, 1.2 % Triton: 
 
5 ml 1 M Tris-HCl, pH 8.0 
1 ml 0.5 M EDTA 
3 ml Triton X-100 
- Bring the volume up to 250 ml with molecular-grade water 
and mix gently to incorporate Triton (this may be done with a 
stir bar and stir plate). 
NOTE: The 250 ml stock of lysis buffer will last for 1 year at 
room temperature (15 - 30°C). 
 
 
3.5.1.2. 
Cell lysis of Gram positive organisms: 
72 
 
==PAGE:73==
 
3.5.1.2.1. 
Label one spin column and two 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes for each 
isolate, and prepare two additional collection tubes per sample. 
NOTE: Only one 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube for each isolate 
is required at this point. 
3.5.1.2.2. 
Add 20 mg/ml of lysozyme to appropriate amount of the lysis buffer 
within 24 hours of use. For example, for 18 isolates: 3400 µl ELB + 
68 mg lysozyme 
3.5.1.2.3. 
Dispense 180 µl of prepared ELB-lysozyme mixture to each labeled 1.5 
ml microcentrifuge tube.  
NOTE: Thoroughly mix  before dispensing. 
3.5.1.2.4. 
Fill a 1 µl inoculating loop with overnight growth (see image below) and 
add to the 180 µl ELB-lysozyme mixture in the 1.5 ml 
microcentrifuge tube, and vortex for approximately 5 - 10 seconds. 
 
 
     
 
3.5.1.2.5. 
Incubate at 56 ± 1°C for 30 min.  
NOTE: Vortexing every 20 minutes throughout the incubation 
process will facilitate and improve cell lysis. 
3.5.1.2.6. 
Add 4 µl of RNase A solution and vortex at medium speed (e.g. speed 
‘7’ on a Daigger Vortex Genie) for 5-10 seconds. 
3.5.1.2.7. 
Incubate at room temperature for 2 min. 
3.5.1.2.8. 
Add 25 µl Proteinase K and 200 µl Buffer AL, and vortex for 5-10 
seconds at medium speed.  
3.5.1.2.9. 
Incubate at 56 ± 1°C for 30 min. 
3.5.1.2.10. Add 200 µl of 95%-100% ethanol and vortex for 5-10 seconds at 
medium speed. 
NOTE: A clear or white precipitate may form on addition of 
ethanol. It is essential to apply all of the precipitate to the 
DNeasy spin column. 
 
3.5.1.3. 
Cell lysis of Gram negative organisms: 
3.5.1.3.1. 
Label one spin column and two 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes for each 
isolate, and prepare two additional collection tubes per sample. 
NOTE: Only one 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube for each isolate 
is required at this point. 
3.5.1.3.2. 
Dispense 180 µl of Buffer ATL to labeled 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tubes. 
3.5.1.3.3. 
Fill a 1 µl inoculating loop with (see above image) overnight growth and 
add to 180 µl ATL Buffer in a 1.5 ml microcentrifuge tube, and 
vortex for approximately 5 - 10 seconds. 
3.5.1.3.4. 
Add 20 µl Proteinase K to each sample tube and vortex at medium speed 
for 5 – 10 seconds. 
73 
 
==PAGE:74==
 
3.5.1.3.5. 
Incubate at 56 ±1°C for 2-3 hours, vortexing every 20 minutes 
throughout the incubation process to facilitate and improve cell lysis. 
3.5.1.3.6. 
Add 4 µl of RNase A solution and vortex at medium speed (e.g. ‘7’ on a 
Daigger Vortex Genie) for 5-10 seconds. 
3.5.1.3.7. 
Incubate at room temperature for 2 min. 
3.5.1.3.8. 
Add 200 µl Buffer AL and vortex for 5-10 seconds. 
3.5.1.3.9. Add 200 µl of 95%-100% ethanol and vortex 5-10 seconds. 
NOTE: A clear or white precipitate may form on addition of 
Buffer AL. It is essential to apply all of the precipitate to the 
DNeasy spin column. 
 
3.5.1.4. 
DNA clean-up and elution: 
3.5.1.4.1. 
Pour the mixture into a DNeasy spin column set in a 2 ml collection 
tube. 
3.5.1.4.2. 
Centrifuge at 10,000 rpm for 1 min and discard the flow-through and 
collection tube. 
3.5.1.4.3. 
Place the DNeasy spin column in a new 2 ml collection tube and add 500 
µl Buffer AW1 (invert buffer several times to mix before use). 
3.5.1.4.4. 
Centrifuge at 10,000 rpm for 1 min and discard the flow-through and 
collection tube. 
3.5.1.4.5. 
Place the DNeasy spin column in a new 2 ml collection tube and add 500 
µl Buffer AW2 (invert buffer several times to mix before use). 
3.5.1.4.6. 
Centrifuge at 13,000 - 14,000 rpm for 3 min to collect the flow-through 
in the collection tube and dry the membrane. Discard the flow-
through and collection tube. 
OPTIONAL: During this step, prepare a tube with enough 10 
mM Tris-HCl pH 8.0 for 100 µl per sample + 1 extra, and 
incubate at 56 ± 1oC while samples are centrifuging. 
3.5.1.4.7. 
Place the DNeasy spin column in a clean, labeled 1.5 ml microcentrifuge 
tube and add 100 µl 10 mM Tris-HCl pH 8.0 directly onto the 
DNeasy membrane. Be sure not to touch the membrane with the pipet 
tip. 
3.5.1.4.8. 
Incubate at room temperature for 1 min.  
3.5.1.4.9. 
Centrifuge at 10,000 rpm for 1 min to collect the eluate in the new tube. 
3.5.1.4.10. The DNA is now ready for quality control. 
 
3.5.2. DNA Quality Control: Quantification Using the Qubit 2.0 Fluorometer and 
Quality check using the Nanodrop 2000 Spectrophotometer 
 
3.5.2.1. 
Quantification Using the Qubit 2.0 Fluorometer 
3.5.2.1.1. 
NOTE: The Broad Range (BR) kit is designed to be accurate for initial 
sample concentrations from 100 pg/µl–1,000 ng/µl. Use for 
quantitation of product containing higher concentrations of DNA (i.e. 
DNA extractions).  The High Sensitivity Kit (HS) is designed to be 
accurate for initial sample concentrations from 10 pg⁄µl to 100 ng⁄µl. 
Use for quantitation of product containing a lower concentration of 
DNA (i.e. PCR product). 
 
74 
 
==PAGE:75==
 
3.5.2.1.2. 
Sample Preparation 
3.5.2.1.2.1. 
Set up and label one assay tube for each sample and the two 
standards.  
3.5.2.1.2.2. 
Prepare the Qubit working solution using a 1:200 ratio of 
Qubit Reagent to Qubit Buffer for each sample and the two 
standards.  See table for an example of calculations.  
NOTE: Store the HS / BR Reagent away from light 
exposure, as it contains fluorescent components.   
 
Working Solution reagents 
1x 
8 samples + 2 standards 
Qubit HS or BR Reagent 
1 µl 
= 10 µl  
Qubit HS or BR Buffer 
199 µl 
= 1990 µl 
Total 
200 µl  
= 2000 µl 
 
NOTE: If desired, increase the number of samples 
used in the calculation by at least one to ensure 
sufficient volume.  
3.5.2.1.2.3. 
For each standard, dispense 190 µl of working solution and 
add 10 µl of the Qubit standards into the appropriately labeled 
assay tubes. 
3.5.2.1.2.4. 
Dispense 198 µl Working Solution and 2 µl of input DNA to 
each sample assay tube. The final volume for each sample and 
standard should be 200 µl.  
3.5.2.1.2.5. 
Vortex all tubes for 2 – 3 seconds. 
3.5.2.1.2.6. 
Incubate all tubes for a minimum of 2 minutes at room 
temperature and read within 1 hr. The short time frame is 
required to minimize the exposure of the reagent to light.  
NOTE: Ensure that the assay is performed entirely at 
room temperature. Do not hold the assay tubes in your 
hand before a measurement, because holding the tubes 
warms the solution and results in a low reading.  
 
3.5.2.1.3. 
Qubit® 2.0 Fluorometer Operation 
3.5.2.1.3.1. 
Touch the screen to activate the device. 
3.5.2.1.3.2. 
When prompted to choose the sample type, select “DNA”. 
3.5.2.1.3.3. 
When prompted to choose the assay type select “dsDNA 
Broad Range” or “dsDNA High Sensitivity” depending on the 
assay used. 
3.5.2.1.3.4. 
When asked whether new standards are available, select “yes”. 
3.5.2.1.3.5. 
Insert Standard 1 and push “read”. 
3.5.2.1.3.6. 
Insert Standard 2 and push “read”. 
NOTE: If the instrument is unable to read the 
standards, start the process over by preparing new 
standards and samples using the instructions outlined 
in step 4.5.2.1.2.1. 
75 
 
==PAGE:76==
 
3.5.2.1.3.7. 
Insert the first user sample and push “read.” 
3.5.2.1.3.8. 
 Once the initial read is complete, push “calculate stock 
concentration” and select 2 µl on the volume roller wheel, in 
the Dilution Calculator Screen (the units should be ng/µl when 
proceeding with Nextera XT library prep). 
 
 
 
 
 
 
  
3.5.2.1.3.9. 
 Push “Save”. A progress bar will appear indicating that the 
displayed data is being saved to the instrument. 
NOTE: The “Save” button can be pushed multiple 
times without creating duplicate entries. 
3.5.2.1.3.10. 
Proceed to the next user sample and repeat steps 4.4.3.1.3.7. – 
4.4.3.1.3.9. until all samples have been read. 
 
3.5.2.1.4. 
Data Transfer 
3.5.2.1.4.1. 
When all samples have been read, push the “data” button at 
the bottom right of the screen.  
3.5.2.1.4.2. 
Insert the flash drive in the designated slot. Highlight the reads 
for the samples of interest and push the flash drive icon on the 
lower left of the screen to transfer the data. A progress bar will 
be displayed to show the status of the process. 
NOTE: A green dot on the USB icon indicates that the 
instrument recognizes the flash drive. If the flash drive 
76 
 
==PAGE:77==
 
is not present, not inserted properly, or cannot be 
recognized, a red dot will be displayed instead. 
3.5.2.1.4.3. 
Remove the flash drive. The saved .CSV file can now be 
opened in Microsoft Excel on any computer workstation. 
3.5.2.1.4.4. 
Samples are listed, from top to bottom, in the order of the 
most recently read to the first read.  
3.5.2.1.4.5. 
Rename the samples accordingly. The default sample names 
under the “Name” column when the file is opened in Excel 
will be the time at which each sample was read.  
OPTIONAL: DNA concentration values can also be 
written down in lieu of using the flash drive, primarily 
for situations where only a few samples have been 
quantitated. 
NOTE: You will need at least 10 ng/µl to proceed 
with library prep. 
 
3.5.2.2. 
Quality Check Using the Nanodrop 2000 Spectrophotometer 
3.5.2.2.1. 
Select the Nanodrop 2000 icon on the desktop of the Nanodrop 
workstation.   
3.5.2.2.2. 
Select the appropriate application from the screen, in this case “nucleic 
acid”, and follow prompts to begin initialization. When asked if you 
would like to open up your last workbook, choose “yes” if you would 
like to append results to previously saved data, or choose “no” if you 
would like to begin a new workbook.   
NOTE: The arm of the Nanodrop must be down during 
initialization. 
3.5.2.2.3. 
Lift the arm of the Nanodrop and use a lint-free laboratory wipe 
dampened with distilled H2O to wipe down the top and bottom 
pedestals.   
3.5.2.2.4. 
Pipette 2 µl of blanking solution (10 mM Tris-HCl pH 8.0) onto the 
bottom pedestal and lower the arm after loading. Ensure that “Add to 
report” is selected in the upper left quadrant of the screen so that 
measurements are saved, and click the “Blank” button on the screen 
(upper left). 
3.5.2.2.5. 
After the instrument has read the blank, lift the arm and wipe both 
pedestal and arm with a dry laboratory wipe to ready the Nanodrop 
for measuring samples. 
3.5.2.2.6. 
Pipette 2 µl of undiluted DNA sample onto the bottom pedestal and 
lower the arm.  
3.5.2.2.7. 
Enter the sample name in the “Sample ID” field (upper right) and click 
“Measure” (upper left). When the measurement has been taken, the 
results will populate the screen. 
NOTE: After the first sample is measured, follow the prompt 
to save your workbook. 
3.5.2.2.8. 
You must save your workbook before continuing.                 
3.5.2.2.9. 
Wipe both pedestals clean with a lint-free wipe dampened with dH20 
and repeat steps 4.5.2.2.6. – 4.5.2.2.9. for all samples.  
77 
 
==PAGE:78==
 
3.5.2.2.10. After all samples have been measured, click on the “Reports” icon in the 
lower left quadrant of the screen to print and/or export data if desired. 
3.5.2.2.11. The value for the 260/280 field (i.e. protein content) should be between 
1.80 and 2.00. 
IMPORTANT: If samples do not meet the 260/280 
requirements, the DNA can be cleaned using the DNA 
Clean & Concentrator-5 kit by Zymo Research (See 
Appendix PNL-2 for detailed instructions). 
3.5.2.2.12. Store DNA extractions to be used within two weeks at 2 to 8ºC.  For 
long term storage, keep extractions at -20 to -80°C.  
 
3.6. Day 1 or 2: 
NOTE: Sample Plate and Sample Sheet setup steps in the Experiment Manager 
program on the Illumina MiSeq can be completed at any point in this protocol, but 
must be performed prior to the start of the run. When sequencing less than 7 samples 
or for newly trained laboratory personnel, we recommend creating the Sample Plate 
and Sample Sheet at the beginning of the library prep. Refer to Appendix PNL-3 for 
detailed instructions on how to complete these steps. 
 
3.6.1. Library Prep 
 
3.6.1.1. 
Enter the 260/280 Nanodrop values, the Genome Size Estimate and the DNA 
concentrations determined from the Qubit BR dsDNA Assay Kit (Section 
4.5.2.1) into the appropriate columns on the Initial Dilution tab of the Nextera 
XT Library Prep Workbook (Appendix PNL-4).  
NOTE1: The genome size estimates for E. coli, Salmonella, 
Campylobacter and Listeria are as follows: 
E. coli and 
Salmonella – 5 million bases; Campylobacter – 1.7 million bases; 
Listeria – 3 million bases. 
NOTE2: The Nextera XT Library Prep Workbook contains two 
worksheets: the Initial Dilution and Normalization and Pooling. 
3.6.1.2. 
Print the Initial Dilution tab to use as a guide for serial dilutions. 
3.6.1.3. 
Label the dilution plate (as shown below) before beginning DNA dilutions.  
 
78 
 
==PAGE:79==
 
 
 
3.6.1.4. 
Follow the dilution directions on the Nextera XT Library Prep worksheet to 
normalize DNA concentration to 0.2 ng/µl, adding water first and then the 
input DNA. 
NOTE: Tagmentation and PCR setup should be performed in a 
clean space separate from all other post-PCR processes in order 
to reduce the possibility of cross-contamination. 
3.6.1.5. 
Pipette up and down approximately 10 times to thoroughly mix each dilution 
before proceeding to the next one. This is VERY IMPORTANT. Accurate 
DNA quantitation is essential for a successful library prep and subsequent 
cluster generation on the MiSeq.  
 
3.6.1.6. 
Tagmentation of Input DNA 
3.6.1.6.1. 
Turn on a thermal cycler before performing the following procedure as 
some steps below are time sensitive.  
3.6.1.6.2. 
Remove ATM and TD from -20°C freezer and thaw at room temperature. 
Store on ice until ready to use.  
3.6.1.6.3. 
Invert the ATM and TD 3 - 5 times. 
3.6.1.6.4. 
Remove the new vial of NT from 2 - 8°C refrigerator. 
NOTE: As a convenience, NT may be stored at room 
temperature near the thermal cycler.  
3.6.1.6.5. 
Visually inspect NT to insure there is no precipitate. If there is a 
precipitate, vortex until all particulates are resuspended.  
3.6.1.6.6. 
Selecting two new lanes (“NTA equivalent” in the above plate diagram) 
from the same plate used for the dilutions, add 10 µl of TD buffer to 
each sample well.  
3.6.1.6.7. 
Add 5 µl of input DNA at 0.2 ng/µl (1 ng total) to each sample well 
containing TD buffer. Change tips between samples. A multichannel 
pipette can be used. 
3.6.1.6.8. 
Add 5 µl of ATM to each sample well containing input DNA and TD 
buffer, changing tips between samples.  
79 
 
==PAGE:80==
 
NOTE: Tagmentation is time sensitive. It is important to 
perform steps 4.6.1.6.2. – 4..6.1.6.14. rapidly.   
3.6.1.6.9. 
Using a multichannel pipette, gently pipette up and down 5 times to mix. 
Change tips between samples. The total volume in each well is 20 µl.  
3.6.1.6.10. Cover the plate (now the NTA plate) with a fresh microseal A. Make 
sure the seal is tightly sealed over the sample wells. 
3.6.1.6.11. Centrifuge the NTA at 800-1200 rpm for approximately 1 minute.   
3.6.1.6.12. Place the NTA in the 96-well block of thermal cycler.  
3.6.1.6.13. Upon initial set up, create and save a “TAGMENT” program on the 
thermocycler with the following conditions: 
 
55°C for 5 minutes 
Hold at 10°C 
 
NOTE: Because this step is time and temperature sensitive, 
do not leave the thermal cycler. TAGMENT run time is less 
than 7 minutes. 
3.6.1.6.14. Run the “TAGMENT” Program. 
3.6.1.6.15. Aliquot 7 µl of NT per sample well into strip tubes during TAGMENT 
run time. 
NOTE: Aliquots of NT may be prepped ahead of time.  
3.6.1.6.16. As soon as the sample temperature reaches 10°C, carefully remove the 
microseal and add 5 µl of NT to each well. 
NOTE: Because this step is time and temperature sensitive, 
use a multichannel pipette to add the NT.  
3.6.1.6.17. Gently pipette up and down 3-5 times to mix. 
3.6.1.6.18. Cover the plate with a fresh microseal. 
3.6.1.6.19. Centrifuge the plate at 800 - 1200 rpm for approximately 1 minute. 
3.6.1.6.20. Incubate the plate at room temperature for at least 5 minutes. 
 
3.6.1.7. 
Amplification of Tagmented DNA 
3.6.1.7.1. 
Remove NPM and the appropriate Index Primers from -20°C storage and 
thaw at room temperature (see Appendix PNL-3 for Dual Indexing 
Principles and Pooling Guidelines). Store on ice until ready to use.  
NOTE: It is not recommended for the indices to exceed 5 
freeze/thaw cycles. 
3.6.1.7.2. 
It is important to maintain color balance for each base of the index 
read being sequenced, otherwise index read sequencing could fail 
due to registration failure. Always use at least two unique and 
compatible barcodes for each index (index 1 and index 2). Indices 
are color balanced in pairs 701/702, 703/704, and 705/706 are 
color balanced as well as 501/502, 503/504, and 505/506. When 
choosing indices for a run make sure you have a set of at least 1 
color balanced index pair per sequencing run (Example: 701/501, 
701/502, 702/501,702/502).The following table illustrates “good” 
and “bad” indexing examples. 
80 
 
==PAGE:81==
 
 
3.6.1.7.3. 
Gently invert tubes to mix and briefly centrifuge. 
NOTE: It is very important to centrifuge the index tubes. 
Liquid can become trapped inside the cap after inverting and 
can be inadvertently lost.  
3.6.1.7.4. 
Add 15 µl of NPM to each well of the NTA containing tagmented DNA. 
Change tips between samples. 
3.6.1.7.5. 
Add 5 µl of the appropriate Index 1 primer (orange caps) to the 
designated wells of the NTA, discarding caps and replacing with fresh 
orange caps as each primer is used.  
3.6.1.7.6. 
Add 5 µl of the appropriate Index 2 primer (white caps) to the designated 
wells of the NTA. Discard the caps and replace with fresh white caps 
as each index primer is used. 
3.6.1.7.7. 
Using a multichannel, gently pipette up and down to mix.  
3.6.1.7.8. 
Securely cover the plate with a fresh microseal A.  
NOTE: This is a critical step. The plate needs to be tightly 
sealed with a microseal to avoid sample evaporation. Using a 
thermal cycler with a tight-fitting lid will ensure that a 
minimal amount of product is lost. 
3.6.1.7.9. 
Centrifuge at 800-1200 rpm for approximately 1 minute. 
3.6.1.7.10. Place the NTA in a thermal cycler. 
3.6.1.7.11. Upon initial set up, create and save a “NAP_XT” program on the 
thermocycler, with the following conditions:   
 
72°C for 3 minutes 
95°C for 30 seconds 
12 cycles – 95°C for 10 seconds 
 
       55°C for 30 seconds 
 
       72°C for 30 seconds 
72oC for 5 minutes  
Hold at 10oC 
50µl per reaction 
Heated Lid  
 
3.6.1.7.12. Run the “Nap_XT” program.  
NOTE: This is a safe stopping point. The plate may remain in the 
thermal cycler overnight or it can be stored at 2 - 8oC for up to two 
days. 
81 
 
==PAGE:82==
 
 
 
3.6.1.8. 
Pre-Clean Up Qubit Quantification  
NOTE: This extra QC step may help troubleshoot if Post Clean-up PCR product 
recovery is problematic. It is also recommended for newly trained laboratory personnel.  
3.6.1.8.1. 
Remove the NTA from thermal cycler or 4oC. 
3.6.1.8.2. 
Centrifuge the NTA for approximately 1 minute to collect condensation. 
3.6.1.8.3. 
Determine the concentration (ng/µl) of each sample in the NTA using 
the Qubit dsDNA HS Assay Kit. (See section 4.4.3.2.2.1., DNA 
Quantification using the Qubit 2.0 Fluorometer for instructions.) 
3.6.1.8.4. 
Record concentrations on the Post PCR dilution page (Appendix PNL-4, 
column D, tab 2) of the NexteraXT Library Prep Worksheet.  
NOTE: Samples for which DNA concentration is below the 
limit of detection should be discarded.  
 
3.6.1.9. 
PCR Product Clean-Up 
3.6.1.9.1. 
Bring the AMPure XP beads and RSB to room temperature. 
3.6.1.9.2. 
Prepare a fresh 80% ethanol dilution. 
3.6.1.9.2.1. 
Approximately 0.5 ml is needed per sample. For 16 samples, 
mix 6.4 ml 100% ethanol with 1.6 ml dH2O. 
NOTE: It is important to always prepare fresh 80% ethanol 
for wash steps. Ethanol can absorb water from air impacting 
sequencing results.  
3.6.1.9.2.2. 
Centrifuge the NTA at 800-1200 rpm for approximately 30 
seconds to collect condensation. (If the optional Pre-Clean Up 
Qubit Quantification was performed, this step may be 
skipped.) 
3.6.1.9.2.3. 
Label a MIDI plate CAA (Clean Amplified Plate). 
3.6.1.9.2.4. 
Transfer 40 µl of the PCR product for each sample from the 
NTA to the CAA.  
3.6.1.9.2.5. 
Vortex the AMPure XP beads until well suspended (~30 
seconds). 
3.6.1.9.2.6. 
Add  20 µl (0.5X volume) of AMPure XP beads to each well 
of the CAA.  
NOTE: Avoid bead carryover by confirming no liquid 
droplets are on your pipette tip. This will affect the 
ratio of beads to PCR reaction and affects the insert 
size.  
3.6.1.9.2.7. 
Gently pipette up and down 10 times to mix. 
3.6.1.9.2.8. 
Incubate at room temperature, without shaking, for 5 minutes.  
3.6.1.9.2.9. 
Place the CAA on the magnetic stand for a minimum of 2 
minutes or until the supernatant has cleared. 
3.6.1.9.2.10. 
With the CAA on the magnetic stand, carefully remove and 
discard the supernatant. 
3.6.1.9.2.11. 
If any beads are inadvertently aspirated into the tips, dispense 
the beads back to the CAA and let the plate rest on the 
magnetic stand another 2 minutes or until the supernatant has 
cleared. 
82 
 
==PAGE:83==
 
3.6.1.9.2.12. 
With the CAA on the magnetic stand, wash the beads by 
adding 200 µl of freshly prepared 80% ethanol to each well.  
NOTE: Do not resuspend the beads at any point 
during the wash steps or remove the plate from the 
magnetic stand 
3.6.1.9.2.13. 
Incubate the CAA on the magnetic stand for 30 seconds, then 
carefully remove and discard the supernatant by pipetting.  
3.6.1.9.2.14. 
With the CAA on the magnetic stand, perform a second 80% 
ethanol wash.  
3.6.1.9.2.15. 
Incubate the CAA on the magnetic stand for 30 seconds, then 
carefully remove and discard the supernatant by pipetting.  
3.6.1.9.2.16. 
With the CAA on the magnetic stand, allow the beads to air-
dry for 10 to 15 minutes. Use a low volume tip to remove any 
remaining ethanol droplets. 
NOTE: Exceeding the maximum air-dry period (15 
minutes) can make resuspension difficult and is not 
recommended.  
3.6.1.9.2.17. 
Remove the CAA from the magnetic stand. 
3.6.1.9.2.18. 
Vortex the RSB tube. 
3.6.1.9.2.19. 
Add 53 µl of RSB to each well of the CAA. 
3.6.1.9.2.20. 
Gently pipette up and down at least 10 times to mix, changing 
tips after each well. 
3.6.1.9.2.21. 
Incubate at room temperature for 2 minutes. 
3.6.1.9.2.22. 
Place the CAA on the magnetic stand for 2 minutes or until 
the supernatant has cleared. 
3.6.1.9.2.23. 
Label a new TCY plate with “CAN” (Clean Amplified NTA 
Plate), the run ID number, initials, and date.  
3.6.1.9.2.24. 
Carefully transfer 50 µl of the supernatant from the CAA to 
the CAN while still on the magnetic plate. Ensure you are not 
transferring any beads as this will affect the subsequent Qubit 
reading. 
3.6.1.9.2.25. 
This is a safe stopping point. If stopping, seal the CAN with 
Microseal ‘B’ adhesive and store at -15 to -25oC for up to one 
month.  
 
 
3.6.1.10. DNA Library QC check and Qubit Quantification 
3.6.1.10.1. Determine the concentration (ng/ µl) of each sample in the CAN plate 
using the Qubit dsDNA HS Assay Kit. (See section 4.5.2.1., DNA 
Quantitation using the Qubit 2.0 Fluorometer for instruction.) 
3.6.1.10.2. Enter the concentrations into the Qubit Output column on the 
Normalization and Pooling worksheet (Tab 2) of the Nextera XT 
Library Prep Workbook (Appendix PNL-5). 
NOTE: The ideal minimum concentration required for 
sequencing is 2 nM. However, a sample can still be run if it is 
below the ideal concentration as long as DNA is detected by 
Qubit. These low concentration samples should not be diluted 
before pooling libraries.  If 25% or more of the samples are 
83 
 
==PAGE:84==
 
below the ideal minimum concentration, consider delaying the 
run, and repeat the library prep procedure for samples with a 
low concentration. These considerations may include 
epidemiological importance or active outbreak investigations. 
 
3.6.2. Setting up a run on the MiSeq 
NOTE: The cartridge takes approximately 1 hour to thaw in a water bath at room 
temperature and once thawed can be stored on ice or at 4°C for up to 24 hours (see 
Appendix PNL-6 for instructions). Alternatively, the cartridge can be thawed in its 
original packaging at 4°C for 8-12 hours, and then stored at 4°C for up to 7 days. If 
thawing using this procedure, proceed directly to step 4.6.2.2. 
 
3.6.2.1. 
Preparing your Reagent Cartridge for the MiSeq 
3.6.2.1.1. 
Retrieve a pre-thawed reagent cartridge and HT1 from refrigerator or 
thaw according to methods in Appendix PNL-6. 
3.6.2.1.2. 
Invert the reagent cartridge ten times to mix the thawed reagents, and 
then visually inspect that all positions are thawed. Be sure the reagent 
in Position 1 is fully mixed and free of precipitates.  
3.6.2.1.3. 
Gently tap the cartridge on the bench to reduce air bubbles in the 
reagents. 
3.6.2.1.4. 
Place the reagent cartridge and HT1 on ice or set aside at 2 - 8oC until 
the sample is ready to load on the cartridge. 
 
3.6.2.2. 
Preparing Reagents and Normalizing the Libraries 
3.6.2.2.1. 
Remove a 100 µl aliquot of 1 N NaOH from freezer and place on ice to 
thaw. 
3.6.2.2.2. 
If library in the CAN plate is frozen, thaw on ice, then centrifuge CAN 
plate at 800-1200 rpm for 1 minute in a centrifuge that accommodates 
microtiter plates. 
3.6.2.2.3. 
Dilute Samples using the Normalization and Pooling worksheet of the 
Nextera XT Library Workbook (Appendix PNL-5). 
3.6.2.2.4. 
For each library, dispense EBT into a clean well of the CAN plate 
according to the volumes listed in the EBT column under Sample 
Dilution.  
3.6.2.2.5. 
Next, dispense the listed volume of each library to the corresponding 
well containing the EBT according to the Sample column. Change 
tips between each sample. 
3.6.2.2.6. 
Mix the CAN plate dilutions by pipetting samples up and down 5-7 
times with a multichannel pipet. 
 
3.6.2.3. 
Pooling the Sample Libraries 
3.6.2.3.1. 
For each sample, transfer the volume listed in the Pooling Volume 
column into a single well on the CAN plate for a total pooled volume 
of 50 µl.  
NOTE: The pooling factor is based on the genome size. When 
genomes of different sizes are run together on the MiSeq, the 
amount of each single library is added proportionately to 
84 
 
==PAGE:85==
 
genome size to reduce the over-representation of small 
genomes in the pooled library. 
3.6.2.3.2. 
Mix the pooled library by pipetting up and down 10 times.  Place on ice. 
 
3.6.2.4. 
Denaturation of the Pooled library DNA  
3.6.2.4.1. 
Add 400 µl of molecular-grade water to the 100 µl aliquot of 1N NaOH 
to make a 0.2 N solution, and invert the tube several times to mix. 
3.6.2.4.2. 
Combine 5 µl of the pooled sample library and 5 µl of the freshly-made 
0.2 N NaOH in a new microcentrifuge tube.  
NOTE: The CAN plate can be sealed with Microseal B and 
stored at ≤ -20°C for up to a month. 
3.6.2.4.3. 
Incubate for 5 minutes at room temperature to denature the DNA. 
3.6.2.4.4. 
IMMEDIATELY add 990 µl of pre-chilled HT1 to the tube containing 
10 µl of denatured pooled library. For the dilution concentration of 2 
nM, 1 ml of 10 pM denatured pooled library is obtained.  
OPTIONAL: The denatured PhiX control may be spiked in at 
this point. See Appendix PNL-7 for instructions. 
3.6.2.4.5. 
Place the denatured DNA on ice until ready to proceed to the next steps.  
 
 
3.6.2.5. 
Dilute to Desired Final Loading Concentration 
3.6.2.5.1. 
Refer back to the Normalization and Pooling worksheet (Appendix PNL-
5) for the dilution concentration (2 nM). Then refer to the 10 pM 
denatured pooled library (from 2 nM dilution) table below to prepare 
the final dilution of the pooled library according to the final loading 
concentration that is appropriate for the instrument and application. 
NOTE: The optimal final loading concentration is determined 
empirically for a particular instrument. Refer to previous run 
metrics for guidance on a target loading concentration. 10pM 
is a good concentration to start with and then increase or 
decrease the concentration until the cluster density falls within 
the 800-1200 K/mm2 target. 
3.6.2.5.2. 
Dilute the pooled library in enough pre-chilled HT1 to achieve the 
desired Final Loading Concentration. 
 
 
10 pM denatured pooled 
library (from 2 nM dilution) 
Final Loading 
Concentration 
6pM 
8pM 
10pM 
Denatured Pooled 
Library  
600µl 
800µl 
1000µl 
HT1 
400µl 
200µl 
0µl 
 
3.6.2.5.3. 
Invert several times to mix the DNA solution. 
85 
 
==PAGE:86==
 
3.6.2.5.4. 
Place the denatured and diluted DNA library on ice until you are ready 
to load your samples onto the MiSeq reagent cartridge. 
 
3.6.2.6. 
Loading the MiSeq and Starting a Run 
3.6.2.6.1. 
Retrieve the Flow Cell and Incorporation buffer (PR2) that are part of 
the MiSeq Reagent Box v2 stored at 4°C. 
3.6.2.6.2. 
Clean the flow cell as follows: 
3.6.2.6.2.1. 
While wearing clean, powder-free gloves, carefully remove 
the flow cell from the container (leave the fluid in the 
container) without touching the glass of the flow cell. 
3.6.2.6.2.2. 
Lightly rinse the flow cell assembly with molecular-grade 
water, making sure that both the glass and plastic casing are 
thoroughly rinsed of the excess salts.  
3.6.2.6.2.3. 
Using care around the black port gasket, pat dry the flow cell 
and cartridge using a lint-free wipe. Take particular care in the 
area of the gasket and adjacent glass, making sure to remove 
any excess fluid. 
3.6.2.6.2.4. 
Wet a clean piece of lens paper with 70% ethanol to clean the 
flow cell glass, making sure that the glass is free of streaks and 
fingerprints, and that the flow cell is completely free of lint or 
tissue fibers.  
3.6.2.6.2.4.1. 
NOTE: Do not add ethanol directly to flow cell and 
avoid getting ethanol on the flow cell port gasket. 
3.6.2.6.2.5. 
Dry any excess alcohol with a lint-free lens cleaning tissue, 
and visually inspect to make sure that the flow cell ports are 
free of obstructions and that the gasket is well-seated around 
the flow cell ports. 
 
3.6.2.6.3. 
Loading the Flow Cell 
3.6.2.6.3.1. 
On the main Sequencing screen of the computer, select 
“Sequence” to initiate “Load Flow Cell” screen.  
3.6.2.6.3.2. 
Raise the flow cell compartment door, and then press the 
release button to the right of the white flow cell latch.  
3.6.2.6.3.3. 
Remove the old flow cell and discard. Visually inspect the 
flow cell stage to make sure it is free of lint. If lint or other 
debris is present, clean the flow cell stage using a lint-free 
tissue moistened with ethanol or isopropanol. Carefully wipe 
the surface of the flow cell stage until it is clean and dry.  
3.6.2.6.3.4. 
Hold the flow cell by the plastic edges near the Illumina label. 
Make sure the label is facing upward and place the flow cell 
on the flow cell stage making sure that it sits flush to the stage, 
and that the two openings are directly over the two prongs set 
in the stage. 
3.6.2.6.3.5. 
Gently press down on the flow cell latch to close it over the 
flow cell. You will hear a click when the flow cell latch is 
secure.  
3.6.2.6.3.6. 
Check the lower-right corner of the screen to confirm that the 
flow cell RFID was successfully read.  
86 
 
==PAGE:87==
 
3.6.2.6.3.7. 
Close the flow cell compartment door. 
3.6.2.6.3.8. 
Select “Next” on the Load Flow Cell screen. The Load 
Reagents screen will open. 
 
3.6.2.6.4. 
Loading the Reagents 
3.6.2.6.4.1. 
Gently invert the capped bottle to mix the Incorporation buffer 
(PR2), and then remove the lid. 
3.6.2.6.4.2. 
Open the reagent cartridge door and raise the sipper handle in 
the right hand compartment until it locks into place.  
3.6.2.6.4.3. 
Remove the MiSeq Wash Buffer bottle, re-cap, and set aside 
for future use. 
3.6.2.6.4.4. 
Place the PR2 bottle in the indentation where the MiSeq Wash 
Buffer bottle was previously located. 
3.6.2.6.4.5. 
Empty the contents of the waste bottle into the appropriate 
waste container, if necessary.  
3.6.2.6.4.6. 
Slowly lower the sipper handle. Make sure that the sippers 
lower into the PR2 and waste bottles. 
3.6.2.6.4.7. 
Check the lower-right corner of the screen to confirm that the 
RFID of the PR2 bottle was read successfully.  
NOTE: If the RFID is not read by the system for 
any step, the software prompts you through the 
steps to obtain a temporary bypass code and 
proceed with setting up the run. For more 
information, see Resolving RFID Read Failure in 
the MiSeq System User Guide. 
3.6.2.6.4.8. 
Select “Next” on the Load Reagents screen. 
 
3.6.2.6.5. 
Loading the Sample Libraries onto Cartridge 
3.6.2.6.5.1. 
Thoroughly dry the reagent cartridge. Again, be sure there is 
no water on the top of the cartridge before proceeding. 
3.6.2.6.5.2. 
Heat the denatured DNA library to 96 ± 1oC for 2 minutes in a 
heat block, followed by immediately cooling in an ice-water 
bath (combining approximately 3 parts ice and 1 part water) 
prior to loading. This will assure all DNA strands are 
denatured. 
3.6.2.6.5.3. 
Use a separate, clean 1000 µl pipette tip to pierce the foil seal 
over the reservoir labeled “Load Samples.”  
3.6.2.6.5.4. 
Using the Rainin RT-L1000XF pipette and corresponding tips, 
pipette 600 µl of the denatured DNA library into the “Load 
Samples” reservoir.  Load into bottom of reservoir; do not 
allow droplets to form on the sides. 
NOTE: Take care to avoid touching the foil seal as 
you dispense the sample. 
3.6.2.6.5.5. 
Confirm the MiSeq screen states “load reagent cartridge” 
and the sippers in the chiller have been raised. 
3.6.2.6.5.6. 
Open the reagent chiller door, remove the wash tray, and dry 
bottom of chiller compartment if necessary using paper 
towels. 
87 
 
==PAGE:88==
 
NOTE: Do not leave the reagent chiller door open for 
extended periods of time. 
3.6.2.6.5.7. 
Hold the reagent cartridge on the end with the Illumina label, 
and slide the reagent cartridge into the reagent chiller until the 
cartridge stops.  
3.6.2.6.5.8. 
Close the reagent chiller door. 
3.6.2.6.5.9. 
Check the screen to confirm that the RFID of the reagent 
cartridge was read successfully.   
3.6.2.6.5.10. 
Close the reagent compartment door. 
3.6.2.6.5.11. 
Select “Change Sample Sheet” to select sample sheet prepared 
previously in Illumina Experiment Manager. 
3.6.2.6.5.12. 
Select “Next” on the Load Reagents screen. The Review 
screen opens. 
3.6.2.6.5.13. 
Start the MiSeq Run 
3.6.2.6.5.13.1. 
Review Run Parameters: review Experiment Name, 
Analysis Workflow, and Read Length. These 
parameters are specified in the sample sheet. Make 
sure to save any changes made. 
3.6.2.6.5.14. 
Select “Next”. The Pre-Run Check screen will open. 
3.6.2.6.5.14.1. 
Review Pre-Run Check: The system performs a check of 
all run components, disk space, and network 
connections before you start the run. If any items do 
not pass the pre-run check, a message appears on the 
screen with instructions to correct the error. For more 
information, see Resolving Run Setup Errors in the 
MiSeq System User Guide.  
NOTE: You will need at least 100 GB disk 
space (20% of the hard drive) before a run can 
be started. 
3.6.2.6.5.15. 
When all items successfully pass the pre-run check, you are 
ready to start your run. 
3.6.2.6.5.16. 
Select “Start Run”. 
NOTE: Once the run has started, do not open the 
flow cell compartment or the reagent compartment 
door, or touch the instrument monitor unless you 
plan to stop or pause the run. The MiSeq is sensitive 
to vibration and touching the instrument during a run 
could cause the run to halt and could adversely impact 
sequencing results. If you need to touch the instrument 
for any reason, pause the run.  
 
3.6.3. Day 2 or 3 
3.6.3.1. 
Exporting Data from the MiSeq 
3.6.3.1.1. 
Record run statistics (i.e. Q30, cluster density, clusters passing filter, 
estimated yield) in the table on the worksheet after the run has 
finished and before proceeding to the post-run wash. 
3.6.3.1.2. 
Data is found in the D drive → Illumina → MiSeqOutput →  Run folder 
(choose the most recent run folder for your data) → Data → 
88 
 
==PAGE:89==
 
Intensities → BaseCalls. Within the BaseCalls folder the raw read 
data is in fastq.gz format, there will be 2 files per isolate for paired 
reads. This data can be copied onto an external hard drive or USB 
drive with sufficient space and moved to a computer workstation. 
Please note that it takes 20 minutes to 1 hour for the MiSeq to 
generate data post run. For Basespace users, the data will be located 
in the run folder on Basespace.  
 
3.6.3.2. 
Post-Run Wash and Reagent Disposal 
3.6.3.2.1. 
Once the run is complete, select the Start Wash option at the bottom 
right-hand side of the screen. 
3.6.3.2.2. 
Prepare a squirt bottle containing the wash buffer (0.5% Tween 20 
solution in molecular grade water) and fill each reservoir of the wash 
tray with the wash buffer. 
3.6.3.2.3. 
Open the reagent compartment door and reagent chiller door and remove 
the used cartridge from the chiller. Set cartridge aside. 
3.6.3.2.4. 
Slide the wash tray into the reagent chiller until it stops, then close the 
reagent chiller door. 
3.6.3.2.5. 
Raise the sipper handle, remove the PR2 bottle and replace with the 
MiSeq Wash Buffer bottle (also containing the 0.5% Tween 20 
solution). 
3.6.3.2.6. 
Remove the waste container and dispose of contents in a chemical waste 
bottle. 
NOTE: The IMP reagent in Position 1 of the cartridge 
contains Formamide, which must be disposed of properly 
through a chemical waste system.  
3.6.3.2.7. 
Return the waste container to the reagent compartment, lower the sipper 
arm, and close the reagent compartment door. 
3.6.3.2.8. 
Select “Next” to begin the post-run wash. This will take approximately 
20 minutes. 
3.6.3.2.9. 
Using a Pipet-Aid and a 1 ml serological pipette, remove the Formamide 
waste from the position 1 reservoir of the cartridge and add to the 
appropriate chemical waste container. Once the reagent has been 
removed, the cartridge can be disposed of in the biohazard waste 
receptacle. 
3.6.3.2.10. The flow cell, wash bottle, wash tray, and waste bottle should always 
remain in place while the instrument is not in use. 
 
3.6.3.3. 
Performing a Standby Wash 
3.6.3.3.1. 
If the machine will be idle for more than 1 week a standby wash must be 
performed. 
3.6.3.3.2. 
Select Standby Wash from the wash options on the screen. 
3.6.3.3.3. 
Fill each reservoir of the wash tray with molecular-grade water 
containing 0.5% Tween 20. 
3.6.3.3.4. 
Open the reagent compartment door and reagent chiller door and follow 
the instructions above for the Post-run wash for proper waste reagent 
removal. If this is following a post-run wash, empty and refill the 
89 
 
==PAGE:90==
 
wash tray and refill the MiSeq Wash Buffer bottle (also containing the 
0.5% Tween 20 solution). 
3.6.3.3.5. 
Once the wash cartridge and MiSeq Wash Buffer bottle have been 
replaced and the waste appropriately disposed of, close the reagent 
compartment door. 
3.6.3.3.6. 
Select “Next” for the wash to begin. This first step of the wash will take 
approximately 20 minutes to complete. 
3.6.3.3.7. 
After the first step of the wash is complete, remove the wash tray and 
refill. Refill the Wash Buffer bottle if necessary and discard the waste. 
3.6.3.3.8. 
Return the wash tray and wash bottle, close the reagent compartment 
door, and select “Next” to begin the second wash. 
3.6.3.3.9. 
The standby wash takes approximately 90 minutes, and once complete, 
the machine may be left idle for 7 days. 
 
3.6.3.4. 
Performing a Maintenance Wash 
3.6.3.4.1. 
A maintenance wash should be performed once a month. 
3.6.3.4.2. 
Under Wash Options select Maintenance Wash and prepare wash 
cartridge and Wash Buffer bottle similarly to the standby wash. 
3.6.3.4.3. 
This is a series of 3 washes that requires refilling of the Wash Buffer 
bottle and wash cartridge after each wash cycle (20 minutes). 
3.6.3.4.4. 
The maintenance wash takes approximately 60 minutes. 
 
3.6.3.5. 
MiSeq shutdown and reboot to maintain virtual memory space 
3.6.3.5.1. 
A shutdown and reboot of the MiSeq should be performed once a week 
after washing the MiSeq and data transfer off of the MiSeq 
3.6.3.5.2. 
On the MiSeq Controller Software select the button “Manage Your 
Instrument” then click “Shutdown”. 
3.6.3.5.3. 
Once shutdown is complete (MiSeq screen is black) flip the power 
button on the back right side of the MiSeq to off, wait 5 seconds (the 
machine will make a faint click), then flip the power button back to 
on. 
 
3.6.3.6. 
Management of Disk Space on D: (Data) Drive of Illumina MiSeq 
3.6.3.6.1. 
The MiSeq requires 100GB of disk space free on the D drive before 
sequencing on the MiSeq can start, data should be cleared from the D 
drive after washing the MiSeq and data transfer of fastq.qz files is 
complete. 
3.6.3.6.2. 
Go to Data (D Drive)/Illumina/MiSeqOutput/(most recent run folder)/ 
3.6.3.6.2.1. 
Within this folder select the “images” folder and delete. 
3.6.3.6.3. 
Go to Data (D Drive)/Illumina/MiSeqAnalysis/ 
3.6.3.6.3.1. 
Delete any run folders including the most recent folder.

 Annotation of CDS with Pfam domains and GO terms 
 Annotation of CDS with Best BLAST hits using predefined or 
custom databases 
Improvements 
 Swapped the Trim Sequences tool and the Optional Merge 
Paired Reads tool in the Data QC and OTU 
Clustering ready-to-use workflow in order to merge more 
identical amplicon reads. This may result in different results 
in some analysis. 
 Improved the tolerance of the Download Bacteria Genomes 
from NCBI tool towards unstable FTP connections with 
NCBI. 
 Enabled graphical export of Bar Chart, Area Chart, Sunburst 
Chart and PCoA Chart vizualisation of abundance tables. 
 Added legends to Bar Chart and Area Chart vizualisations of 
abundance tables. 
 Improved the speed and compute ressource requirements of 
the OTU Clustering tool. 
 The OTU Clustering tool now reverse-complements reference 
OTUs when most reads map in the reverse strand. 
 Improved the length of the trimmed reads output by the Fixed 
Length Trimming tool on datasets with a large read length 
standard deviation. 
 The OTU Clustering tool now produces a summary report that 
can be used to evaluate the quality of the input data and the 
OTU clustering. 
 The Optional Merge Paired Reads tool now produces a 
summary report. 
 The Fixed Length Trimming tool now produces a summary 
report. 
 Activated links to the manual from ready-to-use workflow 
wizards. 
 Updated the UNITE database that is downloaded by 
the Download OTU Reference Database to the latest 
version 
Bug fixes 
 Adapted the Download Bacteria Genomes from NCBI tool to 
a new structure of the NCBI ftp site.

 Fixed a bug in the Fixed Length Trimming tool that caused a 
wrong automatic length calculation when run on inputs with 
a very large number of reads.

Merge Paired Reads tool and theFilter Samples Based on
